Various Organizations

Reports on Flooding in Various Provinces

Gaoyou Fellow Countrymen Association: To the esteemed editors of Shen Bao and other newspapers, Gaoyou is unfortunately beset by frequent calamities. Following the disasters of war, drought, and famine, we now suffer from devastating floods. Since the beginning of summer this year, incessant rains have persisted for months, causing lake and river waters to surge dramatically. Dykes and dams have collapsed entirely, leaving a vast expanse of water. Crops have been swept away, and homes are submerged. The dead float in the water, while the living cling to treetops for rescue. Wails of sorrow echo across the ravaged fields, a scene of heartbreaking pain. Such widespread devastation is rarely seen. We have already telegraphed Chairman Chiang, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Departments of Civil Affairs and Construction, the Central Party Headquarters, the Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters, the China Relief Association, the Chinese Red Cross Society, the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee, various provincial flood relief associations, the Jiangsu Relief Association, and various charitable organizations to report the dire situation and plead for urgent relief. Esteemed newspapers, long regarded as representatives of public opinion and voices of the people, we are now submitting a copy of our telegram and respectfully implore you to lend your powerful support in appealing for aid. May the surviving remnants of our community be given a chance to be reborn. The desperate victims will be eternally grateful. Our association also bows deeply in gratitude. Wang Taomin and others, Standing Committee Members of the Shanghai Provisional Gaoyou Association of Fellow Countrymen, respectfully submit. Enclosed is a copy of the telegram (titles omitted):

To the esteemed editors, Gaoyou is unfortunately suffering repeated calamities. In the years 1927, 1928, and 1929, successive droughts and famines occurred. Even paddy fields near water sources yielded little harvest due to the ravenous consumption of strange insects. Although planting was possible in 1930, the hardships endured from previous droughts and famines made it difficult to sustain livelihoods. The high cost of rice and exorbitant prices for rice seeds further impoverished the people, leaving many unable to purchase seeds and abandoning their fields. Moreover, rampant banditry and extortion became a daily occurrence. The suffering of the people of Gaoyou has been unbearable to witness. We had hoped for a good autumn harvest this year to alleviate their hardships, but unexpectedly, since the beginning of summer this year, continuous rains have caused the Huai River to overflow and the lake waters to surge. The dykes west of the lake have already broken. Although the eastern side is supposedly protected by the Yunhe (Grand Canal) dyke, the river workers have long indulged in self-enrichment in the dyke construction, so the repairs were as if there were no repairs. For example, the Jieshou Small Sluice Gate was in grave danger of collapsing. Despite repeated calls for repairs, the water conservancy authorities remained indifferent. During the recent surge in water levels, the sluice gate suddenly burst. Fortunately, the people of Jieshou risked their lives and spared no expense to build a temporary dam. Many other gate openings have also suffered breaches, causing the lower canals and ditches to overflow early. Combined with days of incessant torrential rain, the water depth in the plains has reached several feet. The current addition of lake swells leads to the simultaneous opening of three dams, which is as detrimental as dam breaks. The vast expanse of water is disheartening to witness. Crops have vanished without a trace, and homes have been swept away by the water. The strong stand on treetops, their cries for help echoing louder than a morning market. The old and weak lie dead on the water surface, drifting east and west, a scene too horrific to bear. The dead are gone, but the living are displaced, without shelter or food, crying out in despair, the fields filled with sorrowful wails, awaiting death. The extraordinary suffering is heartrending. This is the factual account of the devastation in Gaoyou, as reported by various sources. Even more heartbreaking is the information from young men from the disaster area who have come to our association, claiming that the old and weak have drowned and drifted away with the currents, making it impossible to find them. Homes have been washed away and shattered by the winds and waves, leaving no shelter. Some have escaped to Shanghai, seeking work as laborers and requesting our assistance in finding employment to survive. Our association is doing its best to help and provide relief. However, our association is newly established and lacks the resources and credit to do much. Besides introducing them to factories we know, we are at our wits' end and can only lament our helplessness. Alas, the disaster victims who have not found work are crying with hunger in Shanghai. Those coming to our association for assistance number several each day. Without rescue, the number of starving people in Shanghai will increase daily. Without urgent relief, the remnants of Gaoyou will have no hope of survival. All of the above situations are extremely urgent, and we feel compelled to make a heartfelt appeal to seek aid for the millions of disaster victims. Therefore, we humbly and boldly send this telegram to your esteemed office, beseeching you to understand the situation and to allocate substantial funds for the disaster area to provide urgent relief, enabling the suffering and dying victims to have a chance at rebirth. For those who have escaped to Shanghai seeking work, we urge charitable organizations, Shanghai officials at all levels, and factory owners to prioritize the employment of disaster victims from Gaoyou introduced by our association, regardless of wages. A single meal is as good as saving a life. Employing a thousand people is like saving a thousand lives. If this is granted, the disaster victims in both locations will be eternally grateful, and our association will bow ten thousand times in gratitude. Wang Taomin and others, Standing Committee Members of the Shanghai Provisional Gaoyou Association of Fellow Countrymen, respectfully submit.

Emergency Flood Relief Association: The Shanghai Association for Emergency Flood Relief received a telegram from Chen Diaoyuan, Chairman of the Anhui Provincial Government (titles omitted): I respectfully inform you that Anhui Province has experienced continuous torrential rains for more than ten days, causing rivers to rise simultaneously. The magnitude of the floods is unprecedented in decades. Hills have collapsed, valleys have overflowed, dykes have broken, homes have been destroyed, and people are trapped like fish. The land has become a watery expanse. The province also suffers the continuation of banditry. Following hail damage, the province now suffers from floods. Refugees are without shelter, famine is imminent, and families are separated by life and death. I am deeply distressed and cannot find peace, considering the severity of the disaster. I am concerned for the survivors. I have temporarily returned from an inspection tour, passing through Lu'an, Huoshan, Hefei in western Anhui, reaching Wuhu, and various counties along the Yangtze River, up to Huai'ning. The distance of several hundred miles is a vast expanse of water, a giant immersion. Countless people, livestock, and homes have been washed away. I have reviewed disaster reports and telegrams from other counties, with similar pleas for help. The disaster area covers almost the entire province. Wails of hunger and cries of sorrow fill the land. The sights and sounds are deeply disturbing. As the provincial leader, I have done my best to provide relief, but my efforts are limited. I have allocated funds and dispatched personnel to provide emergency relief to alleviate the immediate needs. To organize relief efforts and plan for reconstruction, given the severe shortage of funds in the treasury, the vastness of the disaster area, and the severity of the disaster, a cup of water is insufficient to extinguish a cart of fire, and a robe needs threads from many looms. You have long been known for your kindness and compassion, and your reputation extends far and wide. I have mailed donation ledgers, respectfully requesting your contributions, generously opening your purses, broadly soliciting donations, and eagerly awaiting your response. Your benevolence will be immense, and your virtuous deeds will spread far. I look forward to your prompt response. Chen Diaoyuan bows.

Relief Association: The China Relief Association has received telegrams from the Henan Provincial Relief Committee, reporting that Yanling, Shangqiu, Suiping, Shenqiu counties, Jiangsu's Huai'an and Baoying counties, Anhui's Wangjiang, Xiangcheng, Dangtu, and Hanshan counties have suffered from sudden and overwhelming floods. Lives have been lost to the waves, and homes have been destroyed by the wind and rain. Survivors have no place to escape and no time to call for help. Those fortunate enough to survive are exposed to the wind and sleep in the open, without a full meal for days. Floating corpses lie unburied, causing unbearable grief. The association urgently seeks relief efforts to save the survivors. The detailed and tragic situation is beyond description. The association desires to provide relief but lacks the resources. We trust that charitable people across the country, witnessing the widespread flooding, will have compassion and contribute their strength to save these dying victims.

Chinese Red Cross Society: The Chinese Red Cross Society yesterday continued to receive flood reports from various locations: (1) Hanshan, Anhui: The southwest half of Hanshan is entirely comprised of polder villages, bordered by Chaohu Lake above and the Yangtze River below. Since the beginning of summer, immense floods, accompanied by wind and rain, have arrived together. Simultaneously, over sixty large and small polders have been submerged. The last hope, the Yanglin Great Polder, although defended with all efforts, was ultimately breached on July 28 due to the overwhelming wind, rain, and water. The surrounding fields and homes, extending over a hundred li, have been washed away, leaving nothing behind. What is particularly tragic is that people could migrate gradually away from previous floods. However, this time, the water rushes from head to toe, from top to bottom, making migration impossible. In addition, the area suffered banditry last year, emptying nine out of ten homes in the surrounding villages. Combined with continuous rain during the wheat harvest, the transplanting of seedlings was hindered by water receding and rain accumulating for ten days. The majority of the mortgaged fields are now utterly devastated. Those who drowned have filled the bellies of fish, while the survivors are left naked and desolate, their faces like doves on the water's edge and on tombs. Cries of sorrow and sighs of lament fill the air. Those who did not die by drowning will die of hunger. This is an unprecedented disaster in recent decades, and the most severe calamity among the dozens of counties in Anhui. Being in the disaster area, how can we bear to witness this? We urgently seek relief to alleviate the suffering. We implore all great philanthropists to generously open their purses and for the elders of Anhui to contribute grain. We will bow deeply on behalf of the disaster victims in gratitude for the virtue of rebirth. Sincerely, the Second District Party Department and the Third District Public Office of Hanshan County, Anhui, and the Yuncao Township Chamber of Commerce. (2) Taixian, Jiangsu: To the Shanghai Chinese Red Cross Society, Taixian is unfortunately suffering from incessant rains that began on July 3 and have persisted for an entire month, causing the city walls to collapse in many places and countless homes to be destroyed. The water depth in the plains reaches several feet, and broken walls and ruined fences are everywhere. In the southeastern highlands of the county, boats are sailing on land, and soybean seedlings have been submerged. At that time, there was still hope for the crops in the northwest regions, which could have provided some relief if they had been harvested. Unexpectedly, the lake waters rose again, and the dams along the Yunhe Dyke were opened in succession, pouring water into Xinghua, Taixian, and Dongtai counties, causing even greater harm. According to surveys, the total rice production in Taixian County is approximately four million dan per year, with early rice accounting for about 30% and late rice being the majority. Since the beginning of summer, there have been torrential rains, with autumn weather arriving in summer. The development of crops , If the dams are protected until after the Beginning of Autumn, although the late rice will suffer losses, there is still early rice to harvest. However, with the dams opened before the Beginning of Autumn, the western waters flow directly to the lower reaches of the Yunhe River, directly impacting the northwest regions of Taixian County, becoming the tail end of the Huai River. The harvest of early rice is hopeless, and late rice is even more uncertain. As a result, all crops in the county have suffered damage, and the loss to the people's food supply and economy is immeasurable. Currently, farmers in various areas not only have no grain in their barns and no food in their mouths, but their villages have also become flooded, leaving them with no place to live. The strong scatter in all directions, while the old and weak are left to die in ditches. The tragic situation is beyond description. In addition to convening a Food Management Committee and a Flood Conference to stabilize rice prices, ban the export of rice, and strive for allocation, we dare to make a telegram appeal, respectfully requesting your society to quickly dispatch personnel, with funds, to Taixian to investigate and provide urgent relief, bestowing benevolence upon these survivors and enabling them to live. Sincerely, Pan Lu, Standing Committee Member of the Taixian County Party Department, Zhang , Magistrate of Taixian County, and various affiliated institutions and organizations. (3) Henan Provincial Relief Committee: To the Chinese Red Cross Society, the flooding in Henan Province has only worsened, with the tragic situation beyond words. According to the report from the Magistrate of Yanling County, the terrain of Yanling is low-lying. Since the beginning of summer this year, there have been more overcast days than sunny days. In early June, there were torrential downpours, with water depths in the plains reaching one foot. The villages of Dibai and Conggou were flooded due to the breaches of the Hongye River and Shuangbai River. The villages of Chengguan, Taocheng, and Nanwu were flooded due to the breaches of the Qingliu and Shahe Rivers, creating a vast expanse of water. Many people and livestock drowned, and the autumn harvest was washed away. The terrain of Tongyi County is mountainous, with rapid water flow. People, livestock, food, and clothing were all washed away by the floodwaters. Houses collapsed, and crops were destroyed. Unexpectedly, heavy rains fell again in mid-July, creating a vast expanse of water. The third, fourth, fifth, and sixth districts in the south of the county are low-lying and completely submerged. Taxpayers Association Letter

The Municipal Council Should Not Levy Land Tax on "Fang Dan" Properties

Exercising Municipal Authority Inappropriately by Establishing Private Law for Landowners

The Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers Association wrote to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: We are writing in response to your letter No. 1552 of August 7 regarding the levy of taxes on "Fang Dan" properties, which we have read carefully. This matter is of great importance, and the Association must make the following clarifications to demonstrate that the levy of taxes on "Fang Dan" properties is an extra-legal act that the Council should immediately rectify and cease collecting. (1) The letter states that "there have been many cases of 'Fang Dan' properties paying taxes, as stated on pages 132 and 319 of Volume 1 of Judge Feetham's report, which largely states that 'Fang Dan' properties have never paid taxes." Whether or not "Fang Dan" properties should pay taxes is a legal question that will be discussed later. However, this point alone is enough to shake the confidence in adopting Judge Feetham's report. The levy on Fang Dan property is a concrete fact, while the report uses a very affirmative statement, saying that there was never a levy, this leads to two conclusions. One is that the person providing the facts knows that the levy on "Fang Dan" properties is a legally unauthorized act. If the judge knew this fact, it would make him think that "the principle of the rule of law" could not be said to be observed by the governing bodies of the Public Concession, or two, the person providing the facts to Judge Feetham overlooked it, or thought it was illegal and inconsistent with the principle of the rule of law, so they concealed it and said positive words to promote the law. However, from the first conclusion, the responsibility for not being honest lies with the person providing the facts, and the harm is small. If it is said from the second conclusion, if it is an omission, then Judge Feetham's report has omissions about extremely important facts, other things can be known, then the plan based on these facts can be called a complete error, as the saying goes, one wrong move, the whole game is lost. If it is hiding evil and promoting good, then in the moment of writing, there is partiality in the heart, independence and fairness are just empty talk on paper. (2) The letter states that "it must be read in conjunction with Section 8 on page 133 of the same report," implying that the Association's previous letter was quoting out of context. However, after rereading it, it further strengthens the Association's argument. According to the precedent of Mr. Bonar, a candidate magistrate, on March 4, 1914, which is a precedent of the British court, without the consent and approval procedures stipulated in Article 28 of the Land Regulations, it cannot be legally binding on our Chinese residents. In other words, our Chinese residents are naturally not obligated to comply with this precedent. It is also not true that "'Fang Dan' properties with new buildings will be taxed." "Fang Dan" properties along Tongfu Road, Jing'an Temple Road, and Weihaiwei Road that have new buildings are everywhere where taxes are not paid. Those who pay taxes are only like Gu Shidi and others, who are forced to accept the restrictions of private law behavior under the pressure of a kind of force by those who have authority. (3) The letter states that "it is a fair move to tax 'Fang Dan' properties that have been developed and have greatly benefited from municipal facilities." The Association has long striven for fair moves, but they have not yet been achieved. Various unfair facts are not within the scope of this letter and will not be repeated here. However, the Association believes that unless the procedure stipulated in Article 28 of the Land Regulations is followed, the collection of taxes on "Fang Dan" properties is still legally unfounded. The Association does not wish to see the rule of law undermined. (4) The final paragraph of the letter states, "According to the agreement, the 'Fang Dan' properties of Gu Shidi and Wang Anfu should be taxed." (1) The Association believes that the conditions for paying land taxes attached to this agreement violate the provisions of the Land Regulations and are naturally invalid under the law, just as if a Chinese business owner permanently leased land to a foreigner without the approval of his responsible authority, the lease contract would naturally be invalid under the law. In short, if there is a legally granted power to levy "Fang Dan" taxes, there is no need to use private legal procedures. The collection of land taxes is the exercise of general municipal administrative power, and there is no need to enter into private legal contracts with each landowner. It may be said that contracts are sacred and cannot be violated, but contracts that violate national laws (including international covenants) are deemed invalid and unenforceable in whole or in part, and the same is true for cases similar to Gu and Wang, with no exceptions, for the sake of maintaining the rule of law. We hereby request that you investigate and handle this matter.

Actively Proceeding with Raising Funds for Grain Storage

A Rickshaw Puller Crushed to Death by a Chimney

A chimney at the Zhabei Dacheng Yarn Factory, weakened by violent winds and heavy rain, collapsed suddenly on the 10th of this month, crushing a rickshaw puller. The puller, named Wang Jiaqing, 27 years old, from Funing, was sent to Baolong Hospital for treatment, but died yesterday. Yesterday, his wife, Wang Du, reported the death to the local court. Prosecutor Yang and others arrived at the scene to investigate and order the body to be prepared for burial, pending a thorough investigation into the cause of the collapse before further action.

Worker Crushed to Death by Belt, Skull Fractured

Zhao Huiquan, a worker at the Rihua Yarn Factory on Route Labosheng in Western Shanghai, only 18 years old and from Gaoyou, residing in a bungalow on Binlang Road, was at work at the factory yesterday at around 9:30 AM when he went to the workshop to retrieve something. Inadvertently, his head came into contact with a belt on the machine. The violent impact crushed his skull instantly, causing brain matter to splatter and blood to gush out. He collapsed and died on the spot. Workers in the workshop reported to the factory manager, who immediately sent personnel to report to the Sixth District Police Station and instructed the local neighborhood chief to report to the local court, requesting them to send personnel to inspect the scene.

Mei Lanfang's Novel Obsession

Mei Wan Hua, the "King of Actors", went south this spring to perform at the opening ceremony of the Du Shrine. Mr. Wen Gongda gifted him a copy of "The Official's Family's Fragrant Dream Diary," written by the famous Shanghai novelist Xu Zheshen. Mei Lanfang returned north after his performance, and while on the train, he perused the novel, becoming increasingly amazed. He believed the book possessed a certain artistic quality that could aid him in his theatrical performances. After returning to Beijing, he even enthusiastically encouraged relatives and friends to purchase and read the book. Recently, he sent someone to Shanghai specifically to buy various novels published by Xu, which was learned by Shanghai friends. They praised Mei Lanfang's literary progress and bestowed upon him the title of "Novel Obsessive."

The Development of Bingxun Shorthand

Bingxun Shorthand School is the only Chinese shorthand school in the country that offers both face-to-face and correspondence courses, making it the most complete. The school has refined techniques, a large number of students, and graduates are able to attend and take shorthand notes at major conferences and speeches, such as celebrity lectures at the Autonomous Training Institute and special lectures at the Shanghai Education Bureau's summer school. Since relocating to 168 Sichuan Road, the school's affairs have further developed. Face-to-face and correspondence courses are now advertised for enrollment, taught personally by the inventor, Master Yang Bingxun. The convenient class times, central location, clean classrooms, and low fees make it very attractive, and newspaper reporters and court clerks receive half price as a form of preferential treatment. Enrollment at the Shanghai Bank is very enthusiastic.

Fruits and Local Goods Industry

New Standard Weights and Measures Adopted Today

The Shanghai Fruit and Local Goods Industry Association held a special membership meeting yesterday afternoon to discuss implementing the new standard weights and measures (市斤) system, as ordered by the Shanghai Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau. The following resolutions were adopted: (1) All members shall uniformly adopt the new market standard from August 15th (today). (2) A drafting committee was appointed to prepare a declaration and announcement, which will be printed overnight and distributed to all members for compliance. (3) Ten staff members were appointed to depart simultaneously on the evening of the 14th to collect the old scales and weights from various members for temporary storage by the association to prevent abuses and demonstrate a thorough adoption of the new system. (4) A draft will be submitted to various newspapers for publication to inform fellow businesses in other ports. (5) A letter will be sent to the Municipal Police Bureau requesting protection for each member's market on the 15th to prevent opposition from street vendors. (6) A list of the new standard weights and measures will be prepared and distributed to all members for display in prominent locations in their shops. After the discussions, personnel were dispatched to carry out the decisions, and the meeting adjourned.

Paris Theatre Showing the Film "Long Song Expressing Intentions"

The Paris Theatre on Avenue Joffre, starting today (Saturday), will present the complete singing and dialogue supreme ethical film, "Long Song Expressing Intentions". The film stars Al Jolson, the globally admired singing sage and star of the famous film "The Jazz Singer," and the child prodigy Tan Wanli. It tells the story of a singer who misunderstands his wife, leading to a falling out. Fortunately, their love for their child prevents a formal divorce, but their experiences are heartbreaking and beyond words. The film depicts familial love and the husband-wife relationship in great detail, and its tragic scenes are sure to move audiences to tears. It is more than just a film that relies on fame; it is truly Al Jolson's best work. Such a wonderful film is worth seeing even in the sweltering heat.

The Renowned Military Telescope of Sincere Company Manager

The optical department manager of Sincere Company, Mr. Hensoldt of Germany, produces various military telescopes. Even at a thousand miles away, objects can be seen as if they were only a few steps away. During the European War, General Hindenburg specially ordered the factory to temporarily prohibit sales, which shows the importance of this telescope for military purposes. It is exquisite, compact, and easy to carry, and the price is very affordable. It is currently managed by the company and is selling very well.

News Regarding Parcels to Hankou and Airmail to Hanyi

Postal authorities state that airmail service between Hankou and Yichang will be suspended for two weeks starting August 10th. They also state that because steamships between Hankou and Yuejiakou are temporarily out of service, parcels that were previously transported by them must now be transported by rail and by porters on land. Therefore, all parcels sent to the Hankou area and to other locations that were normally reached via Hankou, with the exception of Caidian and Hanchuan, will be subject to an additional pure fee charged to the recipient upon arrival.

Letter to the Editor

To the Esteemed Editor: I recently read your report about Madam Sun's arrival in Shanghai. I was quite surprised by the section "The New Sound Society Reporter Talks with Madam Sun's Accompanying Secretary, Ms. Hu Lanqi, Former Member of the Jiangxi Provincial Government." Firstly, Lanqi accompanied Madam Sun on this trip to China in a friendly capacity and was not serving as her secretary. Secondly, Lanqi previously ran relief efforts in Jiangxi and was not a member of the provincial government. I am specifically requesting a correction to avoid reader misunderstandings. Respectfully, Hu Lanqi, August 14th.

Education News

Important News

Zhejiang Province Has Not Approved Registration of Private Schools

Ministry of Education's Handling Measures

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education reported to the Ministry of Education that all private secondary schools in the province, except Mingde Middle School in Jiaxing, have followed regulations and applied for registration. Currently, over thirty schools have been approved for registration by the Provincial Department and have been reported to the Ministry for record. More than ten schools, including Huangyan Fuya Junior High School and Jiangshan Hejiashan Junior Agricultural Vocational School, have also repeatedly applied for registration. However, due to unfamiliarity with the laws and regulations, there are many omissions in the reporting procedures. Furthermore, funding is insufficient, resulting in inadequate equipment. Although the Provincial Department has instructed these schools to make corrections, they still do not fully comply with the Ministry's regulations for registration, and thus cannot be immediately approved. The reason for this is different from those who are deliberately waiting and seeing. However, with the deadline approaching, the schools have been ordered to suspend enrollment in the first semester of the 20th academic year to show seriousness and provide supervision. However, since suspension of enrollment is different from closure, guidance is requested on how to handle this.

The Ministry of Education, after receiving the report, instructed the Provincial Department: "The reports are all noted. Since it is stated that Huangyan Fuya Junior High School and Jiangshan Hejiashan Junior Agricultural Vocational School have repeatedly applied for registration, they are not to be compared with those who are deliberately waiting and seeing. Although they do not fully comply with the registration standards, they should be given an opportunity to improve. As it is stated that after the deadline, the situation will be carefully examined, and either an order will be given to complete the process by a certain date, or they will be advised to convert to other types of schools, with the hope of greater improvement. It is proposed to extend the trial period (up to one academic year). The handling is not inappropriate. Those who have already started the registration process but have not yet submitted the forms to the Provincial Department, or have been instructed by the Provincial Department but have not yet replied, should be urged to submit their replies quickly before the registration deadline. The Provincial Department should consider the situation and handle them separately according to the above methods. As for Mingde Middle School in Jiaxing, if it still does not complete the registration procedures by the deadline, it should be ordered to close down to uphold the law. You must comply with this instruction and keep a copy of the report. This order."

Ministry of Education Schedules

Meeting of the Vocational Education Design Committee

The Ministry of Education has scheduled the first meeting of the Vocational Education Design Committee for 9:00 AM on September 1st. Notices have already been sent to all committee members. Any committee member who has proposals should submit them to the Ministry three days before the meeting, along with five vocational education topics: (1) Discussion of methods for training teachers for all levels of vocational schools; (2) Discussion of standards for establishing vocational schools; (3) Discussion of standards for establishing departments in vocational schools; (4) Discussion of internship methods for vocational schools; (5) Discussion of vocational guidance methods for primary and secondary schools.

Ministry of Education Clarifies Education Association Issues

The Ministry of Education received a telegram from the Anhui Department of Education stating that the format of documents used by education associations at all levels has not been clearly stipulated. Furthermore, Article 19 of the Education Association Law stipulates that higher-level education associations should have their directly subordinate education associations as members. Therefore, are members of lower-level education associations also members of their directly higher-level education associations? Should the annual fees be paid to the county association, or should they also be paid to the district association to which it belongs? The Ministry of Education replied: Regarding the mutual correspondence between education associations at all levels, the central government has recently ordered a review by the Executive Yuan, and it has been reported that education associations at all levels are different from administrative organs. It is proposed that the format of official documents should be official letters. After the instruction is approved, it will be ordered to be followed. Furthermore, the tenth-level education association should have its directly subordinate education association as a legal entity, not the members of the lower-level education association. Therefore, individuals are also members of their directly higher-level education association. All members of the district education association should pay their membership fees separately to their respective district education associations and should not pay their membership fees directly to the county or city education associations. You must be informed and instructed to comply accordingly.

Questions Regarding Jinling University's Agricultural Science Enrollment Qualifications

Ministry of Education Has Clearly Explained

Jinling University presented to the Ministry of Education the question of whether graduates of Category A agricultural old-system middle schools and old-system normal schools who have served in society for more than two years after graduation are qualified to apply to the school's agricultural vocational program. The Ministry of Education instructed that, according to Article 24 of Chapter 5 of the University Regulations, the entrance qualification for vocational programs requires graduation from a senior high school or equivalent school and passing the entrance examination. Therefore, graduates of Category A agricultural old-system middle schools and old-system normal schools who have served in society and have equivalent academic qualifications are not eligible to apply. You must be informed.

Local News

Municipal Bureau of Education

Strictly Investigate Private Schools Claiming to be Registered

The Minde Primary and Secondary School, a private school on North Sichuan Road in this city, has not yet been approved for registration by the Municipal Bureau of Education. However, it printed the words "Registered by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education" on the cover of its constitution. The Municipal Bureau of Education recently discovered this and considered the school to be fraudulent and deceptive, which is highly inappropriate. A severe reprimand was issued, and the school was ordered to send the constitutions with the printed registration words to the Bureau for destruction. It was also ordered to follow the procedures for applying for registration according to the regulations. If it refuses to comply, it will be shut down. It is also reported that the Bureau is sending personnel to secretly investigate private schools that have not yet started the application process.

Finals Will Be Between China and Japan

Free Talk

A Word or Two

— Qi Chan

The ways of the world change with wealth and influence, more so than with poverty and lowliness. The heart of jealousy is found more often within families than among outsiders.

Observe the hustle and bustle with a cool eye, and you will save yourself much trouble. Approach loneliness with a warm heart, and you will gain endless true joy.

The desire to seize profit and power is a bottomless pit, difficult to fill with ten thousand fathoms. The ambition to love the country and avenge its humiliation is regrettably only five parts full.

Women of ancient times were admired for their rustic charm. Women of today are admired for their modernity.

Those who embrace celibacy are surely those who have lost in love. Those who advocate birth control are surely those with a house full of children.

Do not speak of integrity to those who are obsessed with power and wealth. Do not discuss elegance with the vulgar. Better to remain silent than to speak and invite disaster.

The word "loss" is something that, if practiced throughout one's life, can be endlessly beneficial.

The pen of a lawyer, the blade of a warrior, and the tongue of a prostitute are all inauspicious things in this world.

Those who hate evil like the enemy are bound to suffer激变. Those who do not contend with the world will live out their natural years.

Young people today must be intelligent but not flaunt it, and talented but not boastful, only then will they have the strength to shoulder heavy responsibilities and travel far.

Retire from service when at the height of your powers, and live in a place that is secluded and quiet.

Powdered faces take the stage, with singing and music as loud as boiling water. Soon, the music ends, the crowd disperses, and the stage is empty. Everything in the world should be viewed in this way.

The Strange and Magnificent Siemens Factory

— Xu Shiqi, sent from Berlin

The day after I arrived in Berlin, I drove to visit the Siemens factory with my wife, Manhua, thanks to an introduction from Liang, the acting chargé d'affaires at the Chinese embassy in Germany. The factory is located in the western suburbs of Berlin, covering a wide area, hence the name Siemensstadt. There are elevated trains and trams that connect directly to the outside world. It is one of the largest factories in Germany.

The factory started in 1847, founded by Werner von Siemens, who initially ran a small electrical manufacturing business with a capital of only 20,000 marks and employing only 10 workers. Gradually, it developed, and in 1883, it moved to the suburbs and built its own factory buildings. Now, after 84 years, the number of workers has reached 110,000, and the capital has increased to 220,000,000 marks. Its electrical products, ranging from large items such as郵船, airplanes, railroads, bridges, and machine parts, to small items such as household electric stoves, electric cookers, and electric fans, are sold to countries all over the world. Its spirit of rapid progress is truly admirable.

During our visit, we were warmly received by Mr. F. Pohl, the chief engineer. Mr. Pohl spoke English, French, Italian, and other languages fluently. He led us to visit the exhibition hall, which was surrounded by various models, from the original generators to the latest equipment, all of which were available. The main hall displayed a bust of the founder, Mr. Siemens. He looked like an old man, reminiscing about the hardships of starting the business and his spirit and perseverance. We then visited the manufacturing department and saw various applied electrical machines that had been made, all kinds of them, constantly changing. I was not familiar with mechanical engineering, but I was amazed by the perfection of the equipment and the strictness of the organization.

At noon, the factory provided lunch. The dishes were very exquisite. According to Mr. Pohl, the factory kitchen uses electricity and can cook meals for 4,000 people in one hour. The power of electricity is evident here. Then, we went to a high building to get a bird's-eye view of the whole city. The factory buildings were lined up and the chimneys were everywhere. After that, we visited the kindergarten attached to the factory, which was used to educate the children of the workers. Other facilities, such as sports, entertainment, and housing, as well as all aspects of life, work, childcare, illness, and insurance, were all taken care of meticulously. We were also given exquisite publications as souvenirs.

The spirit of German science is sweeping the world. Recently, due to overproduction, worker unemployment, and economic exhaustion, it has reached this point. However, the spirit of patience, perseverance, and perseverance can break through difficulties and rebuild. It is an excellent example for us to work hard.

Japanese Discover Historical Relics in Korea and Manchuria

— You Xu

Japanese archaeological expert Dr. Kanai Yasuyama traveled to Manchuria last winter and collected many ancient artifacts from China and Korea. Recently, the doctor came to Hangzhou to travel and brought many kinds of ancient artifacts and ancient books. All the antiquarians rushed to visit him to get a glimpse first. According to the doctor, he has been researching historical sites in Korea and Manchuria for nearly twenty years and feels that the historical relics of Korea are the most difficult to collect. Now, he has unexpectedly found hundreds of historical materials, which is beyond his expectations. He also said that he found more than 130 kinds of inscriptions in Manchuria, most of which have not been discovered by the world. When he was in Manchuria, he and his colleagues Kin'ichiro Yagi and Nagaki Miyoshi obtained the consent of the consul-general in the area and engaged in excavation. Countless ancient coins, ancient mirrors, and ancient bronzes were discovered. In Ningguta, south of what was once the capital of the kingdom of Bohai, which was originally the eastern capital of the Jin dynasty, now called Dongjingchengzi, many ancient tiles and bronzes were unearthed. In Ningguta, they also found a bronze seal from the Jin dynasty and armor from the time when the Qing dynasty originated, all of which are rare treasures. Among the ancient books he brought, the most appreciated by antiquarians are the following: (1) Biographies of People, 80 volumes. (2) Selections from Eastern Literature, 80 volumes (3) Collected Bronze Inscriptions, 16 volumes (4) Bamboo and Wooden Slips of Genuine Works, 6 volumes (5) The Remnants of the Fire (History of Power Struggles in the Joseon Dynasty), 10 volumes (6) The Complete Works of Hongjae (Royal Compositions of King Jeongjo) (7) Records of the Court and Countryside (from King Taejo to King Sukjong). (8) Comprehensive Overview of the Court and Countryside (from King Taejo to King Gyeongjong). (9) Burgeoning History (from King Taejo to King Munjong). (10) Complete Korean Version of the History of Goryeo. Other rubbing copies of steles, such as the victory monument of the Qing Taizu's defeat of the Ming army in the east of Fushun, the inscriptions of the Jin Dynasty's "进士及第", and ancient bronzes, ancient tiles, and ancient coins, can all provide scholars with reference and have great value in history. It is a pity that they are all in the hands of the Japanese. How painful it is!

A Letter to My Third Sister

— Xu Bibo

That night, I got on a rickshaw with this heavy suitcase and a jar of sweet sauce, which was very inconvenient. The rickshaw puller probably hadn't eaten enough dinner, so he walked with a sway, and the swift legs turned into a slow pace. He was also so poor that he didn't even have a rickshaw lamp, and he just walked from a dark and remote place. When he happened to pass through a narrow alley, the rows of flesh on both sides (that is, those who were cooling off shirtless) often scolded him sharply for being uninteresting. I was also repeatedly sweating for him for no reason.

In the process of darkness, I caught a glimpse of the North Temple Pagoda by the light of the lightning. After arriving at the station, I hurriedly handed the return ticket to the porter, signed a delivery note, and hurried through the tunnel. The gigantic behemoth that swallowed Yunmeng also spewed white smoke and wriggled westward.

The train started. The cool wind in the sky did not treat people differently. It did not take sides and gave me, who was uneasy, a lot of coolness. However, the lovely North Temple Pagoda was getting farther and farther away.

Just as I was feeling lost and wondering, a girl in the next seat suddenly frowned and shouted "Hang Yu". I was very surprised and asked her. She said, "I have a headache, dizziness, and stomachache." I knew she must have had heatstroke, so I quickly poured the Chunzai Dew in my pocket into a teacup and gave it to her. In about ten minutes, she was suddenly all right. She thanked me and asked my name. But I was stunned because helping someone in need on the road is a very common thing, and there is no need to tell my real name. So I casually said, "Chen Kengran." I knew this lie would make me embarrassed later.

"Oh, Mr. I'm very sorry. How is your company developing recently? The day before yesterday, I saw in the newspaper that your wife, Ms. Qin Fang, was injured in the face by a stone. Has the scar healed now?" She asked me絮絮地like this.

I was really僵 at that time. I braced myself and simply told a big lie, hoping to stop her question. I said, "This is the advertising effect of the new film "The Dancing Girl's Blood". In fact, there is no such thing."

She was still unwilling to stop talking. She asked, "I heard that "The Dancing Girl's Blood" was written by the detective novelist Mr. Cheng Xiaoqing. Is that right? Who is the male lead?" She asked me like a waterfall. I guess this lady is also a迷咧.

"Speaking of the male lead, it is the famous Lin Xuehuai." I replied to her like this, answering every question. "?…"?…". "?…". She asked so many questions. But I pretended to doze off and ignored her.

I arrived at my residence at 11:30. My mother was still not asleep. But the home-style flavor that her old man longed for, sweet sauce, became a lost item of an unknown person in the train. This is really a pity and regretful thing.

Travel Notes from India (81)

— Ling Hua

9th. During my time in India, apart from new cultural encounters, I also learned several key principles regarding animal psychology. I am now compiling them to demonstrate that the origins of war do not stem purely from materialism, but also from the physiology of the male sex. 1. Darwin stated that competition among male animals arises from vying for females, termed sexual selection. This differs from Marx's view. 2. I learned from an English lady about the example of male cats castrating kittens. 3. I learned from a Muslim scholar about male bears killing their cubs. 4. Also, from a monkey park, I learned about the example of male monkeys killing females. 5. Furthermore, I learned that male peacocks (i.e., purple-crowned chickens, found in Sichuan) steal their mothers' eggs to eat. It is also known that male birds like ducks and geese do not care for their chicks. Thus, the responsibility of nurturing young offspring is a motherly duty. 7. It is also known that mother hens can incubate duck eggs and are equally responsible for protecting those not born from them. All these key principles prove that world wars are caused by the initiation and organization of the male sex, and the underdevelopment and suppression of motherly nature and maternal rights. Marx also explained that some material inequalities can be resolved through the principles of neutrality and fairness, achieving moderation. Even the great power of influence, an invention of Indian psychology, should be adopted to nourish the human spirit. Marx's historical materialism is like giving food to the hungry, while the new spiritual liberation of India's Gandhi is lofty and far-reaching, free and generous, enough to provide humanity with the air to breathe, allowing narrow-minded societies to see the vastness of the universe, the height of the sky, the depth of the earth, the profundity of the sea, the light of the sun, the splendor of the moon, and the beauty of flowers, plants, wind, water, and nature. An Indian told me that capitalists cannot have a conscience, and it is difficult to become a capitalist with a conscience. Gandhi used influence to transform them. Nevertheless, using both material and spiritual means aligns with the Chinese ideal of moderation, which is also Dr. Sun Yat-sen's theory of regulation. To compare and equate everything, achieving complete equality, is indeed very difficult.

India has many beautiful gardens. One had a deer, as large as a big sheep, weighing about eighty catties. I asked someone about its price, and they said it was only five to seven yuan. I imagine in China, it would cost dozens or even hundreds of yuan. I wanted to bring it back, but the shipping fee was too expensive. Someone said that peacocks are worthless in some places, cheaper than chickens in China. Yet, we Chinese regard peacocks as phoenixes. Truly, things are valued for their rarity. There will surely come a day when gold is worth the same as dirt.

In a school, there is a pagoda made of marble, where incense and flowers are offered morning and evening. I asked a student, "Which deity is this?" He replied, "This is the goddess of wisdom, named Saraswati." I asked, "Do all schools have this?" He said, "Most private schools have it, but government schools may not." I note that Greece also has a goddess of wisdom, who is also female. Chinese books like "Dream of the Red Chamber" and "Flowers in the Mirror" advocate that women's wisdom surpasses that of men. Indian books say that women are four times as intelligent as men. According to this, it proves that if the world is to be guided by true wisdom in the future, we must study women's education. Perhaps this is why Indian schools venerate the goddess of wisdom.

Rotary Club Report

Women, Women (20)

— Yao Su Feng

Mr. Li was originally a busybody, and when he heard that the woman outside was looking for Lu Rongqing, he naturally felt he had to get to the bottom of it. They went outside together and saw the woman still sitting outside the guardhouse, her face full of disappointment and anxiety, silently wiping away her tears.

The group of people stopped in front of her.

"Why are you looking for Lu Rongqing? What is he to you?" Mr. Li asked directly.

"Lu Rongqing is my husband…" she only answered this one sentence, the rest of her words choked by tears.

As soon as Mr. Li heard that Lu Rongqing was her husband, he felt it was a very important discovery. He thought to himself that his opportunity for revenge had arrived, and he felt greatly relieved.

He deliberately said to her, "It's no use looking for him here. To be honest with you, Mrs…. Mrs. Lu! Your Mr. Lu has found a good place in Shanghai. Unless you go there to find him…" Mr. Li laughed coldly a few times. The group of people also started to discuss, some feeling strange, some feeling miserable, and those who knew about Mr. Lu and Miss Ding felt that this was a good show to watch.

"Yes! I know, and I have seen him. He has a woman in Shanghai! That's why I came to ask him. Thank you, gentlemen, can you take me to him? I would be very grateful!" she said, her voice full of tears.

"Since that's the case! Then I'll tell you! The woman's surname is Ding, she lives at 1452 Tongfu Road. It's not convenient for me to take you, so I'll hire a car to send you there!" Mr. Li said with a smile.

Lu Rongqing's wife, hearing that her husband had been located, stood up and thanked Mr. Li several times, following him out of the school gate. Mr. Li hired a rickshaw for her, paid the fare in advance, and sent Mrs. Lu to find her husband. As she got into the car, Mr. Li shouted loudly, "Remember! Surname Ding! 1452 Tongfu Road! A small Western-style house! There's a tree in front of the door!"

The rickshaw pulled away. Mr. Li was naturally very pleased. Turning back, he said to the group of onlookers, "Okay! You just wait! There's probably going to be a lively palace coup at our queen's place!" He laughed heartily as he spoke.

The group of people understood the meaning. Several people, upon hearing that this matter was related to Miss Ding, the school's "queen," wanted to follow to see what would happen. However, Mr. Li stopped them, saying, "Let's go hear the news tomorrow! If we go now, everyone will lose face!"

Gold Market Before Swap

Result Slightly Lower by Two Taels

Some Had Already Done Swaps: Yesterday, the gold market, with 14 bids, started firm but then weakened. The situation was generally stable, with slight fluctuations. From morning till night, there were differences of about six taels. In the end, it continued to fall by two taels. Trading was still not substantial. The early morning rise was probably due to the reported decline in silver prices. Subsequently, major players sold off heavily. When the foreign exchange rate initially stabilized, the situation became weak. It briefly broke through the 770-tael mark, but then buyers seemed to increase, and it became milder. The afternoon market continued its downward trend with very slight fluctuations. Finally, it ended at slightly above 71 taels. The swap period has arrived. However, since the 16th falls on a Sunday, it was brought forward by one day, starting at 8:00 AM this morning. However, most of those eager to do swaps had almost finished by yesterday afternoon. Upon learning of this, the exchange immediately intervened to enforce the regulations and prevent private trading. However, with so many people and the chaos, unofficial transactions were unavoidable. It is said that some had already mutually agreed on swaps based on the listed price, with the seller paying out three taels.

The incoming and outgoing of silver and public money orders for money shops was more than 53 million, the incoming and outgoing of foreign public money orders was more than 6.4 million, the incoming and outgoing of foreign draft money was more than 1.9 million, the incoming and outgoing of silver draft money was more than 3.9 million, and the incoming and outgoing of various remittances was more than 700,000, with tens of thousands in cash. According to bank incoming and outgoing statistics, the incoming and outgoing of draft money for Chinese businesses was more than 2 million, the incoming and outgoing of draft money for foreign businesses was more than 1.2 million, and the incoming and outgoing of various goods, exchange rates, taxes, and miscellaneous items was 8.89 million. Incoming warehouse was 800,000, and outgoing warehouse was 300,000. The incoming and outgoing of various items for Japanese banks was more than 3.3 million, and the incoming warehouse was 400,000. The foreign currency transaction volume for small money shops was 780,000. The morning small foreign currency in Jiangnan was 6 qian, 4 fen, 9 li and a half, and the afternoon was 6 qian, 5 fen. The morning transaction volume was 3,500 yuan, and the afternoon transaction volume was 7,000 yuan. The morning small foreign currency in Guangdong was 6 qian, 4 fen, 4.5 li, and the afternoon was also 6 qian, 4 fen, 4.5 li. The morning transaction volume was 175,000 yuan, and the afternoon transaction volume was 35,000 yuan. Copper coins were changed to 1,500 coins, totaling 377,500 coins.

Securities: Seven and Eight Month Term Suddenly Rises by One and a Half Yuan

Unified Tax Nearly Good at Nine Jiao, Other Also Tending to be Firm

Yesterday, spot bond transactions continued to be extremely sparse. Although many term transactions opened, other than the Unified Tax 20 series, the rest were still very quiet. The trend of bond prices continued to be extremely sluggish. However, due to demand exceeding supply, it turned firmer than before. As a result, only the Whole Six series continued to be weak. The remainder, such as the Unified Tax, rose by nearly nine jiao, the 20 series rose by six jiao, and others also rebounded by about two jiao. The seven-year, eight-month term rose by as much as one and a half yuan compared to the beginning of the month. The total value of futures contracts was only over 8.9 million yuan.

Yarn and Cotton Markets Fluctuating and Unpredictable

The yarn market started rising but fell at noon. Recent changes have been rapid, making it difficult to predict. Speculators are unusually enthusiastic, with varying degrees of increase and decrease. However, large players sell heavily when prices rise, overwhelming the market. In reality, the cotton market is poor, and the yarn market also fluctuates. Market sentiment is tighter this month, as the Yunnan group is actively buying 10-count coarse yarn, with asking prices exceeding 3.4 taels. However, the future situation is difficult to grasp.

Human Label Starts Bright, Weakens at Noon: The Human Label opened with a slight rise in American cotton. Retail investors bought in, and market sentiment was firm. Each price rose by 7 or 8 qian. In the afternoon, raw cotton trended down, and the market suddenly fell by 6 or 7 qian to 1 or 2 qian. A total of 44,400 bales were traded. It was found that Ruidai sold 3,000 bales, Changfeng 1,850 bales, Jifeng 1,300 bales, and Deji 1,100 bales. Gongtai bought 1,400 bales, Rongxing 2,100 bales, Gengfeng 2,800 bales, Hengyi 1,300 bales, and Yichang 1,450 bales. The closing prices are recorded below:

Yarn Sales Still Not Bad: Sales of current yarn are still good. According to statistics, various groups bought a total of 1,300 bales throughout the day. The same industry bought 420 bales, domestic customers bought 250 bales, Shantou bought 55 bales, Qingdao bought 175 bales, Yunnan bought 855 bales, and miscellaneous groups bought 60 bales, it is said.

Cotton Market Trends from Flat to Low

The cotton market was flat in the morning but fell at noon, changing very rapidly. However, major players sell as much as possible when prices are high. In the afternoon, rumors circulated in the market that the US Department of Agriculture and various state governors would destroy one-third of American cotton. There was great fear that this would not happen, so market sentiment was very weak, and many retail investors closed out their positions, causing the market to fall sharply. The future situation is still difficult to improve significantly.

Han Label Chaos: The Han Label opened with a slight rise in American cotton, and people's hearts were still calm. Each month was flat. In the afternoon, due to bad news about American cotton, each month fell by 5 or 6 qian. A total of 133,500 dan were traded. It was found that Dafu sold 3,900 dan, Hengda 16,300 dan, Ruidai 6,000 dan, Tongxing 2,000 dan, and Xincheng 3,100 dan. Shenchang bought 2,400 dan, Jifeng 5,500 dan, Gongtai 3,500 dan, and Yichang 5,500 dan. Yi Yu and others bought 3,400 dan. The closing prices are recorded below:

Cotton Demand Mediocre: Trading of current cotton is still mediocre, it is said.

American Cotton Recovers After Short Covering

American Cotton Rebounds by 25 Pounds: Yesterday, American cotton was initially firm due to good news from Liverpool, then weakened due to large-scale selling, and finally rose again due to short covering. Futures rose by 28 to 31 points. Spot rose by 25 points. British cotton futures rose by 12 or 13 points. Spot rose by 20 points. Egyptian cotton spot rose by 15 points. Indian cotton was firm due to short covering and good news from Liverpool. Pingguoer rose by 4 rupees, Aomula rose by 5.5 rupees, and Bairoxi rose by 5.75 rupees. Rice, East New Japonica, Small Drop of Half a Yuan

South Market: Yesterday, the sources from various gangs arrived at approximately 26 or 27 ships. Combined with yesterday's remaining stock in the port, there were over 40 ships in total. As urban and rural shops observed the continuous arrival of goods, the market showed signs of slackness. Moreover, there were reports of firmness in the North Market, resulting in few transactions. The accumulated stock felt even more stagnant. The market prices did not open yesterday due to the extended grace period in the North Market, which caused a significant difference between the North and South. Today, the market was re-evaluated, and prices increased compared to yesterday and the day before. However, the overall trend is softening, and people are closely monitoring the situation. Recently, the price of foreign rice has slightly weakened, making a small correction in the future not surprising. It is rumored that Zhejiang province has imposed a ban on transportation, and the inland stocks are weak, making it difficult for prices to fall.

New Wharf: Yesterday, around 40 boats carrying clams and other goods from Changshu and Xixi arrived. The morning market was quite active. Various shops and firms are buying up stocks in light of the end of the small month on the Gregorian calendar, which will lead to prices going up, and due to the relatively low price of rice. 3,000 bags of thin rice were added to the market, causing the price to rise by six or seven jiao compared to before. Nearly 1,000 shi of thick Japonica rice were sold retail at two or three chi above the price. Lu Yang top grade and "Bian Yuan Wei" were slow, with fluctuating prices. Yesterday, 200 bags of Pudong new Japonica rice arrived, but trading in this street was stagnant, with a drop of half a yuan.

Foreign Rice Drops Two to Three Jiao Again

Tianjin Merchants Slightly Stocking Up

Yesterday's foreign rice market showed no signs of recovery. The current high prices are due to the impact of the floods, with merchants from the Yangtze River region buying heavily, followed by local firms and hoarders. No. 1 Saigon rice jumped to over sixteen yuan, and all grades increased sharply, with prices flying up by over five yuan compared to when foreign rice first arrived in Shanghai. As the floods in various areas receded slightly, the amount of rice purchased was sufficient for use. New river rice has arrived in the city for supply, making merchants unwilling to pay high prices for purchases. The market saw a drop, with prices gradually falling by one or two yuan. Yesterday, Japanese customers continued to show little interest, and the existing stock was sufficient. Ordered goods are on their way and will arrive soon, making people even more bearish. Morning observations indicated a sharp downward trend. Merchants from Tianjin began to take advantage of the situation and slightly stock up on Min Dang rice. Local firms and retailers also followed suit by stocking up on Annam Japonica and small-grain rice, which helped stabilize the market. However, compared to 500 bags at fourteen yuan and a half to thirteen yuan and eight jiao, 1,000 bags of Kolkata rice at fourteen yuan, 300 bags of Annam Japonica rice at fifteen yuan and three jiao, and 300 bags of small-grain rice at thirteen yuan and eight jiao and a half, the prices were still relatively high.

Futures Flour Finally Falls

Yesterday in the flour market, after the opening of trading in the morning and afternoon, the market for various months generally showed a flat and weak trend. As quoted prices for foreign wheat dropped again by a small margin of one or two jiao or so, insiders and outsiders believed that the factories would continue to place orders for foreign wheat, and the chips thrown out were all solid goods. Moreover, the excessive supply abroad would not decrease due to the increased demand in China. The bulls, concerned about this, could not avoid feeling discouraged. Therefore, the bulls in the area of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway gradually withdrew their positions, with only merchants from the Yangtze River region continuing to aggressively buy in, reaching around 300,000 bags. However, with most people bearish, the price finally fell. As a result, August and September fell by one and a half fen compared to the previous day, October fell by one fen and two and a half li, November fell by a small two and a half li, and December and January fell by a small five li.

Futures Wheat Is Weak and Stagnant

Yesterday's futures wheat market, after the opening of trading in the morning and afternoon, showed a generally weak and stagnant trend for various months. Since the large bull operators in the current month had completely sold off their positions at the high prices, the current bulls are all inexperienced, resulting in a force that is no match for the bears, who are gradually reducing the prices. The prices for the distant months were inevitably weak due to the oversupply of foreign wheat, causing many to actively sell off their positions. As a result, both August and September fell by three fen compared to the previous day, while October to December fell by four fen. Spot wheat is in a tight situation due to the lack of incoming shipments. 2,100 bags of Kai Yi Wei, Shuangfeng, Anting, Pudong, Weiting, Penglai Waigang wheat were handled by Fuxin Huafeng.

North-South Goods, Lanxi Jujubes Arrive Fresh

Fresh Lanxi jujubes have continued to enter the market, with good quality. Yesterday, the wholesale market called out a selling price of forty taels. Other grades continued to follow the usual trend of price reductions, and the trend was relatively stable. Top-quality goods have not yet arrived, but new goods are expected to appear in a few days.

Silk and Tea, Double Cocoon Long Filaments Priced High

Price opened at one hundred and sixty-four taels: The price of double cocoon cocoons continues to rise firmly.

This year, the production of double cocoon cocoons in various regions of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces has been poor, while the demand from double cocoon silk factories has increased. In addition, Japanese firms took the opportunity to raise prices and search for purchases, causing cocoon prices to rise. The price of double cocoon long filaments is also firm and high. Yesterday, Sanjin Silk Factory purchased 15 dan of double cocoon silk long filaments at a price of one hundred and sixty-four taels.

European Firms Replenish Yellow and White Factory Silk

Yesterday, the local foreign firm silk market showed no signs of recovery in European sales. Overseas silk telegrams showed little activity in Shanghai. Only English and French firms replenished their stock of yellow and white factory silk. Jardine Matheson and others imported 20 bales of white factory silk and 10 bales of Sichuan yellow factory silk, with prices remaining firm.

Luzhuang Zhenmei Rises Again and Again

Yesterday, in the local foreign firm tea market, Zhenmei green tea from Wuyuan and Tunxi, handled by firms such as Jardine Matheson, Harmony, Jinlong, and Tongfu, seeing that the existing stock in the market was low, the supply was scarce, and the overseas demand was urgent, once again began to actively search for purchases. Top-grade Zhenmei with stems rose to two hundred and fifty-six taels, Wubei Zhenmei rose to one hundred and seventy-eight taels, and Tunxi ordinary Zhenmei rose to one hundred and thirty taels, an increase of twenty-thirty taels compared to before. The upward trend was like a rapid rise to a high position. Other items such as Needle Mei, Xiumei, and bulk tea also saw a uniform increase of five or six taels. Even Gongxi, which in recent days has been purchased by many traders to be reworked into other export grades, has seen a firming trend in the market. The tea market has shown a very stable trend.

Piece Goods, Crossing the River for Banquets, Broadcloth Sales Are Brisk

Recently, there has been demand for Yuan Chang's plain broadcloth in blue-gray, especially with the Sichuan merchants being the most active. The ordinary two liang two or three qian grades are particularly scarce and sell well. Ning Feng's banquet broadcloth number one, two, three, and four sold over ten boxes yesterday, all from the firm's existing stock. Wholesale prices are two liang two qian eight and a half fen net for plain color, two liang three qian five fen for blue-gray, and one liang nine qian for dark green. The market sales are quite smooth, and customers continue to demand more. It is heard that the firm's new goods have not yet arrived in Shanghai, and the stock in the warehouse is limited, so they will soon increase the price by several fen per yard.

Social News

Marshal Foch's Diary of the European War

— Translated by Gu Angruo

Another question discussed at this meeting was that the Allied forces must end this great war in 1919. In a letter I sent to Mr. Clemenceau the other day, I asked him to organize the new recruits of the 1920 class into teams starting in October 1919, for the following reasons:

"1919 will be the decisive year of the Great War. In the spring of that year, the strength of the American army will reach its peak. If we want to shorten the war, our army must step up its fierce attacks from then on. We must pay attention to the Allied forces obtaining sufficient replenishment and maximum supply." I said at the end, "The stronger our army is, the faster the victory will be, and the more we will be listened to."

On July 24, I wrote to all commanders in the same vein, asking them to list the reliable manpower, guns, airplanes, tanks, and military transport vehicles of each army at the beginning of 1919.

I particularly emphasized that not only should we maintain but also expand the superiority of our army's tanks and artillery. Therefore, I asked the commanders to urge their respective governments to step up the construction of such urgently needed military equipment.

On July 26, Commander Pétain expressed his agreement with the war plan in writing and added his opinion, arguing that our army's offensive on the Saint-Mihiel salient "and the clearing of Amiens should be the main goals in the offensive taken in late summer and early autumn. The strength of the French army in 1918 may be exhausted, but this is expected to achieve useful and certain results."

The other two commanders did not provide written replies other than verbally agreeing.

The Allied forces began their offensive in August 1918.

The Allied forces are now preparing to begin the second offensive on August 8.
